D. Project Costs and Financing
3.21      Cost.  The total cost of the project is estimated at US$26.9
million equivalent, net of taxes and duties, with a foreign exchange
component of US$17.2 million, or 64Z of the total project cost. Base cost
estimates, based on January 1989 prices, have been updated to reflect price
levels in February 1990. The table below summarizes project costs by
component. Project costs by component and expenditure category are shown
in Annex 3-5; detailed cost tables are set out in Annex 3-6.
Component                                                Cost
(US$ million)
1.  Employment generation                                    4.0
2.  Improvement of PHC and social services                   6.9
3.  Improvement of N'Djamena's sanitation infrastr.          7.5
4.  Strengthening of social policy planning                  2.9
5.  Project Coordination and Support Unit                    1.0
Total base costs:                                       22.3
Physical contingencies                                   2.0
Price contingencies                                      2.6
Total estimated project costs:                          26.9
3.22      Contingency allowances.  The physical contingency allowance of
US$2 J million equivalent, or 9Z of the estimated total base cost, includes
unfoieseen physical additions for civil works, furniture, equipment,
vehicles, training, and specialist services. Price contingencies of US$2.6
million equivalent, or 12Z of total base cost, were based on an estimated
local annual inflation rate of 3Z for local costs between 1990 and 1995 and
on forecasts of international inflation of 4.9Z for foreign-supplied goods
in the same period.
3.23      Incremental operating and recurrent costs.  The project would
finance incremental operating costs associated with (a) maintenance of
buildings, materials, equipment and vehicles; (b) expanded survey and
research programs; and (c) essential drug distribution. At the end of the
project, annual incremental recurrent costs generated by the project
(excluding the Project Coordination and Support Unit) would amount to: (a)
US$300,000 equivalent per year in wages and materials to continue the
programs defined in the employment-generation component (paras 3.05-3.07);
and (b) US$500,000 in non-wage expenditures (excluding essential drugs) to
continue the other programs. Funds needed for the purchase and
distribution of essential drugs in N'Djamena and Tandjile, estimated at
US$1.0 million at the end of the project, should be covered by the cost-
recovery scheme to be developed under the health component (paras 3.09 and
3.10). Proceeds from a market tax (para 3.14) should cover costs incurred
by the sanitation services.



- 21 -
3.24      Project financing.  The funding sources for the prcject have
been identified, and the financing arrangements were finalized during
negotiations. The proposed IDA credit of US$13.4 million would finance 50Z
of the total project cost. Local contributions total US$1.3 million
equivalent, or 52 of the project cost: the Government would finance 202 of
the project's incremental operating costs, equivalent to US$0.6 million,
and local communities would contribute US$0.7 million equivalent for their
participation in various project components. The following donors would
participate in the financing of specific project components in the form of
grants: Swiss Development Cooperation would cofinance the components to
improve PHC and social services and to strengthen social policy
formulation, for US$6.7 million equivalent; UNCDF would finance specific
activities under the component to improve N'Djamena's sanitation
infrastructure for approximately US$3.2 million (para 3.15). USAID would
finance on a parallel basis the credit assistance and management support
sub-component for approximately US$2.3 million, excluding US$0.6 million
for the incremental credit requirements (para 3.05) to be funded by IDA.
IV. PROJECT IMPLEMENTATION
A. Status of Project Preparation and Readiness
4.01      Composition of the Social Development Action Project was agreed
between the Government and IDA in June 1988. IDA's assistance in preparing
this project was requested by the Government during preparation of the
Financial Rehabilitation Credit (para 2.02) and in connection with the
country's request for participation in the Social Dimensions of Adjustment
(SDA) Regional Program (para 2.21). Pre-appraisal of the project took
place in October 1988 and appraisal in January 1989. Representatives of
all donors participated in the appraisal mission in January 1989. A post-
appraisal mission visited Chad in November 1989. Under the Project
Preparation Facility (PPF), an amount of US$750,000 was approved in April
1989.
4.02      The three studies financed by the SDA Regional Facility (para
2.06) provided the basis for preparing the project and identifying seve-al
of its components. During appraisal, discussions were held with NGOs with
ongoing activities in Chad, similar to those to be undertaken in the
project, in order to benefit from their experience. The action plans for
each component were discussed, with the first year of the training program
defined. Final architectural designs for a rehabilitation and/or
construction civil works program for the health facilities and sanitation
infrastructure were approved by the Government and IDA. For N'Djamena's
health/social services network (para 4.12), nine sites have already been
acquired by the Ministry of Public Health and the Ministry of Social
Affairs and Women's Development. These sites were identified during
appraisal mission and found acceptable. Preparation of bidding documents
for the civil works to be undertaken during the first year of the project
are being financed under the PPF and will be completed by credit
effectiveness. PPF funds are also being used for setting up all executing
agencies and a Project Coordination and Support Unit, as well as for the



- 22 -
hiring of long-term technical assistance to prepare, together with local
staff, a detailed implementation plan for each component. All technical
assistance, with the exception of the specialists for the sub-component on
technical assistance for micro-enterprises (para 4.10) and for the
Sanitation Infrastructure Unit (para 4.14), has been contracted to two NGOs
and two consulting firms with ongoing activities in Chad. The recruitment
process for the remaining specialists has been initiated.
B. Project Management and Coordination
4.03      The project would be implemented under the overall supervision
of the Minister of Planning and Cooperation. An Interminister!al Committee
has been established under the chairmanship of the Minister of Planning to
guide implementation of the Government's social action programs and make
the necessary policy recommendations. Individual executing agencies would
be responsible for Lnplementing each sub-component under the technical
supervision of the relevant ministries, but a Project Coordination and
Support Unit (PCSU) has been set up in the Ministry of Planning to
supervise the financial and procurement aspects of project implementation
and provide support to the executing agencies in their relations with the
donors. The management and coordination arrangements of the project are
detailed in Annex 4-1.
4.04      Interministerial Committee.  The Interministerial Committee is
composed of the following Ministers (or their representatives): Interior
(MI), Finance (MFI), Food Security (MSA), Labor and Employment (MTE),
Public Health (MSP), National Education (MEN), Trade and Industry (MCI),
Public Works (MTP), Regional Urban Development and Housing (MATUH), and
Social Affairs and Women's Development (MASPF). The Interministerial
Committee would meet at least twice yearly to (a) review progress reports
from the executing agencies, (b) approve progress and annual reports on
project implementation and assess prospects for implementing the project's
annual action plans, and (c) review and finalize policy recommendations
based on the findings of the project studies and surveys. The Chairman of
the Interministerial Committee would be assisted in his functions by the
PCSU, the General Directorate, the Human Resources Department, and the
Permanent Secretariat of NGOs of the Ministry of Planning. Specifically,
the PCSU would prepare the Interministerial Committee's meetings, follow up
on its decisions, and ensure quality control of the documents to be
transmitted to the Committee, in particular the annual progress reports.
The documents would be drafted by the executing agencies and reviewed by
four technical sub-committees: for employment promotion, urban
infrastructure, health and community participation, and social dimensions
of adjustment. These sub-committees, which have already been established,
comprise representatives of the relevant Ministries and are chaired by the
Directors General of MCI, MTP, MASPF and MPC, respectively. They would
review and amend, as necessary, the draft annual progress reports and
discuss any relevant policy recommendations that may arise during project
implementation. During negotiations the Government gave assurances that
the Interministerial Committee and the four technical sub-committees will



- 23 -
be maintained throughout the project period, under terms and conditions
satisfactory to IDA.
4.05      Project Coordinatioa and Support Unit.  As an autonomous entity
under the supervision of the Minister of Planning, the PCSU has been
established for the five-year project period to perform the following
functions: (a) consolidate the semiannual progress reports on project
execution and the annual reports on project implementation and
expenditures; (b) prepare annual budgetary programs aggregating the annual
action plans updated by each executing agency; (c) ensure that all bidding
documents and procurement and disbursement matters conform to the
procedures of the relevant donors and that required audits are carried out
in a timely fashion; (d) serve as a liaison between IDA/the other donors
and the executing agencies; and (e) review any contractual disputes that
may arise and refer them to the proper authot'ties. A Project Director and
a Deputy Director have beer. appointed. The PCSU also includes an
experienced accountant and four support staff. After the first three years
of project implementation and until project compi.etion, the PCSU staff
would be reduced to comprise only the Project Director, the accountant and
one support staff member. During negotiations the Government gave
assurances that (a) the PCSU's work procedures and relations with the
executing agencies will be as agreed with IDA; (b) the PCSU will be staffed
for the entire project period with personnel occupying the full-time
positions of Project Director and accountant, and for the first three years
will also include a Deputy Director; and (c) these positions will be filled
at all times with personnel whose qualifications and experience are
satisfactory to IDA.
4.06      Executing agencies.  The individual executing agencies that
would implement the project sub-components would be relevant administrative
unics of the technical ministries concerned, except for the credit and
assistance sub-component that would be implemented by an NGO (para 4.09).
The administrative units would be assisted by additional NGOs and
consulting firms to strengthen their implementation capacity. All NGOs and
consulting firms would be under contract with the Government specifying
(i) the tasks to be performed and their time frame, with the first year's
action plan fully specified, (ii) the accounting, auditing and reporting
procedures to be followed, (iii) the staff profile, and (iv) any conditions
deemed necessary by the Government and IDA in view of the particular tasks
and/or characteristics of the executing agency. During negotiations the
Government gave assurances that the organization, functions, staffing and
responsibilities of the Health-Social Unit and the Sanitation
Infrastructure Unit will be satisfactory to IDA.
4.07      Monitoring, reporting and evaluation.  The procedures for
project supervision and administration are described in detail in
Annex 4-1, and a supervision plan, agreed during negotiations, is at
Annex 4-5. Monitoring of project activities would take place at several
levelst from the executing agencies that implement the project sub-
components to the PCSU as a coordinating entity, with the Interministerial
Committee responsible for the overall monitoring function. Each executing
agency would be responsible for monitoring implementation of its sub-



- 24 -
component, on the basis of detailed indicators included in the annual
action plans related to its sub-component, by (a) each month assessing
performance on the basis of the specified indicators, (b) preparing the
semiannual progress reports, and 'c) updating the annual action plans
related to its sub-component on the basis of performance achieved during
the year under review. The PCSU would (a) consolidate the semiannual
progress reports, and (b) prepare annual progress and financial reports, as
well as annual budgetary programs aggregating the annual action plans, for
annual project reviews to be undertaken with the Government, IDA and the
other donors. A final project evaluation would be carried out during the
last year of the project to analyze lessons drawn from implementing
specific action plans. These lessons would be discussed in workshops and
seminars to be organized at the end of the project and would be reflected
in recommendations for defining future social policies (para 3.18). The
procedures, including the monitoring indicators, have been agreed with the
Government. During negotiations the Government gave assurances that it
will (a) submit to IDA for review annual reports on project implementation
and expenditures, the first report by September 30, 1991; (b) with IDA and
the other donors, undertake annual reviews of the progress of
implementation, starting not later than November 1, 1991, and by November 1
every year thereafter; (c) agree with IDA, not later than December 31 of
each year, on the next annual budgetary program aggregating the annual
action plans for each component and each executing agency; and (d) submit a
project completion report to IDA within six months of the credit closing
date.
4.08      Implementation schedule.  Most of the project's planned
activities, comprising the first three components, is expected to be
implemented over a three-year period. The component for strengthening
social policy formulation is expected to take five years, due to
implementation requirements of the integrated household survey. The
project is expected to be completed by December 1995. The project
implementation schedule is shown in Annex 4-2.
C. Implementation of the Project Components
1. Stimulation of Employment Generation
4.09      Credit assistance and management support.  The technical sub-
committee for employment promotion, chaired by the Director General of MCI,
would be responsible for the supervision of this sub-component, which would
be implemented by the NGO in charge of executing the USAID program (para
2.17). The NGO's performance was reviewed jointly by IDA and USAID staff
to assess the feasibility of its participation in the execution of the sub-
component. Its performance was found to be satisfactory, and USAID will
continue to utilize this NGO as the executing agency. Specifically, the
NGO would be responsible for training local staff to develop their capacity
to operate the credit assistance scheme. In addition, the local staff
would participate in training seminars in Chad and abroad, which the NGO
would organize. The NGO would provide long- and short-term technical
assistance for promotion of an outreach micro-credit program and general



- 25 -
marketing. With regard to management of the line of credit to be funded by
IDA, the NGO would be under contract with MPC; lending terms and
conditions, technical assistance, and credit-processing arrangements for
the three credit windows (para 3.05) were finalized during negotiations.
The NGO would a1so prepare progress reports for the Interministerial
Committee every six months. During negotiations the Government gave
assurances that (a) the interest rate under the credit scheme will be 12Z
until June 30, 1991, and increased to 131 thereafter, with an added front-
end service fee of 22 in both cases; (b) the interest rate will be adjusted
not later than December 31, 1991, on the basis of the findings of a banking
sector review study and pursuant to the financial performance of the credit
scheme and the prevailing commercial interest rates; and (c) the contract
with the NGO for management of the line of credit will be as agreed with
IDA. Conditions of credit disbursement on this sub-component are that (a)
the USAID grant has become effective, and (b) the contract with the NGO lor
management of the line of credit has been signed.
4.10      Technical assistance for micro-enterprises.  A small unit, to be
established within the Ministry of Labor and Employment (MTE) for the first
three years of the project, would implement this sub-component, with
technical supervision being provided by the techmical sub-committee for
employment promotion. A Coordinator would be recruited internationally for
18 months to help establish the unit. He would train a national specialist
(36 man-months) to take over his coordination functions at the end of his
contract. Both would organize and supervise program implementation,
prepare outreach and demonstration techniques, promote technology transfer
and purchase of adapted equipment, and prepare semiannual progress reports
for the Interministerial Committee. The unit would also be staffed with a
local team of three instructors and support staff. Three specialists would
be hired through the Association Francaise des Volontaires du Progres
(AFVP) (72 man-months) to train the three instructors. Dissemination
seminars would be organized for the instructors and managers of workshop
facilities (para 3.06). A condition of credit effectiveness is that the
Coordinator has taken up his duties.
4.11      Counselling for laid-off public employees.  MTE's National Labor
Department (ONAMO) would be responsible for implementing this sub-component
in N'Djamena and Moundou in the cotton zone. An economist would be
recruited locally for 36 months to assist the Moundou branch, as well as
support staff. Ad-hoc consultancy assistance would be contracted for 20
man-weeks to (a) help define, adjust and internalize counselling methods,
as needed; (b) undertake an analysis of the labor market in the N'Djamena
and Moundou regions; and (c) give in-service training to staff.
2. Improvement of Primary Health Care and Social Services
4.12      Restructuring and expansion of N'Djamena's PHC and social
services network. This sub-component would be implemented by a Health-
Social Unit, which has been established under the supervision of the
Director General of the Ministry of Public Health (MSP) in consultation
with the Director General of the Ministry of Social Affairs and Women's



- 26 -
Development (MASPF). Its work would be coordinated by a full-time Senior
Physician from MSP's Hospital and Urban Medicine Department, assisted by a
full-time social worker from MASPF's Department of Social Affairs; both
have been transferred to the Health-Social Unit and have taken up their
duties. The Unit would also be staffed with an Administrator and support
staff. Specifically, the Health-Social Unit would (a) consolidate
essential drug orders from the health centers, purchase essential drugs
through international competitive bidding by using the Central PharmAcy's
infrastructure, and monitor the prescription and distribution of drugs and
the cost recovery scheme; (b) supervise on a regular basis the functioning
of all health facilities to be restructured under the project, particularly
the new integrated health-social centers; and (c) monitor the action
programs for each urban district. These programs would be closely linked
to those to be undertaken in the rural zones of the Chari-Baguirmi medical
region, to which the urban districts are administratively attached.
The Public Building Department of the Ministry of Public Works (MTP) would
be responsible for the technical supervision of the constructLcn and/or
rehabilitation of health and social centers. To achieve this sub-
component's objectives, in particular its emphasis on testing the essential
drug scheme and integrating the activities of health and social personnel,
the Health-Social Unit would be assisted by a full-time public health
specialist and a full-time social worker/nurse (36 man-months each), with
44 man-months of short-term assistance, to be provided by a consulting
firm. The consulting firm would orgarize retraining seminars for health
center managers and health and social personnel. During negotiations the
Government gave assurances that (a) the three integrated health-social
centers, three maternity centers and three dispensaries to be built in
N'Djamena will be staffed as agreed with IDA and located on the sites
already found acceptable; (b) a cost recovery scheme based on a system of
fixed fees per new episode of illness will be introduced for the services
provided by the three maternities constructed under the project and in the
health centers supplied with essential drugs under the project, and will at
all times be satisfactory to IDA; and (c) the Health-Social Unit will be
staffed at all times with personnel whose qualifications and experience are
satisfactory to IDA. It also gave assurances that the Government's
operating budgets for N'Djamena's PHC and social services network will be
increased, starting from their 1990 base, by at least 1OZ each year in
1991, 1992 and 1993, a rate in line with the budgetary provisions under the
third PFP 1990-92. Signing of a contract with the consulting firm,
satisfactory to IDA, is a condition of credit effectiveness.
4.13      Strengthening of regional health services in Tandiile.  This
sub-component would be implemented using the same institutional and
management framework as the one for an, ongoing EDF-financed health project,
which is satisfactory to IDA (para 3.10). Supervision would be provided by
MSP's Director General of Health, with assistance from the consulting firm
responsible for implementing the EDF project, who would be under contract
with MSP. Specifically, this firm would provide long-term technical
assistance to the regional Chief Physician through a Deputy Chief Physician
and a specialist in public health management, each for 36 man-months. The
specialist in public health management would help implement the essential
drug and cost-recovery programs and would train a national counterpart (24



- 27 -
man-months). The firm would also twice yearly organize in N'Djamena and
Tandjile training seminars for health personnel, as well as field
supervision visits. During negotiations the Government gave assurances
that the Government's operating budgets for Tandjile's health services will
be increased, starting from their 1990 base, by at least 10X each year in
1991, 1992 and 1993, a rate in line with the budgetary provisions under the
third PFP 1990-92. Signing of a contract with the corsulting firm,
satisfactory to IDA, is a condition of credit effectiveness.
3. Improvement of N'Diamena's Sanitation Infrastructure
4.14      To implement this component, an autonomous Sanitation
Infrastructure Unit has been established under the technical supervision of
the Ministry of Regionial Urban Planning and Housing (MATUR). Its staffing
is provided by the Governmer.t and comprise a Director, two engineers, two
head foremen, and a specialist in public hygiene; support staff would be
financed under the project. The technical personnel have been transferred
to the Unit and have taken up their duties. In addition, an engineer and a
head foreman, with confirmed experience, would be internationally recruited
to strengthen the Unit (60 man-months). The engineer would define with the
technical staff of the Unit an in-service training program tailored to
their needs. The Unit would (a) handle contracts for architectural and
engineering services from preparation and review of bidding documents, call
for tenders and bid opening to supervision of civil iorks; (b) provide
technical assistance to small contractors participating in civil works;
(c) help improve garbage collection by municipal services; and (d) set up
an analytical accounting system to improve the management of equipment,
tools and spare parts of the force account brigade. The Unit would verify
construction progress and certify payment requests, as well as carry out
maintenance activities of the tertiary drainage network. Personnel both
transferred to or involved in the project would, at the end of the project,
be used to constitute a strong public sanitation and public hygiene
department. The Unit would also supervise implementation of the community
participation program (para. 3.13), for which an NGO with ongoing
activities in Chad would be contracted. The NGO would provide 55 man-
months to organize and implement the program, with co-mmunity development
agents' assis Lance. During negotiations the Government gave assurances
that the qualifications and experience of the technical personnel of the
Sanitation-Infrastructure Unit and the arrangements with the municipal
services will at all times be satisfactory to IDA. Conditions of credit
effectiveness are that (a) the engineer and head foreman recruited for the
Sanitation Infrastructure Unit have taken up their duties, and (b) a
contract with the NGO responsible for the' community participation program,
satisfactory to IDA, has been signed.
4. Strengthening of Social Policy Planning
4.15      The technical sub-committee for the social dimensions of
adjustment would supervise the implementation of this component. The
Applied Research Center (CRA) of the Ministry of Higher Education would be



- 28 -
responsible for implementing the program of studies, which would be carried
out by a team of internationally recruited (30 man-months) and local (37
man-months) specialists. The Department of Statistics (DSEED) of the
Ministry of Planning would undertake the household surveys, with support
from a team of internationally recruited (11 man-months) and local (250
man-months) specialists. The Ministry of Planning's Directorates of
Planning and of Investment would be responsible for preparing policy
papers, which would take into account the findings of the studies and
surveys and lessons from implementing specific action plans, in order to
recommend policy reforms and replicable and sustainable investment
projects. These findings would be submitted to the Interministerial
Committee, through the SDA technical sub-committee, following annual
seminars and/or workshops gathering all parties concerned (including NGOs)
to discuss issues and conclusions and make recommendations. During
negotiations the Government gave assurances that, before undertaking the
socioeconomic studies and household surveys, it will submit for I)A's
approval the annual programs, including terms of reference, schedule, and
arrangements for their dissemination and implementation. It also gave
assurances that it will review with IDA the recommendations of the policy
studies and agree on action plans for their implementation.
D. Environmental Impact
4.16      The project's environmental impact would become progressively
beneficial through the emphasis placed on making the living environment of
disadvantaged groups more healthful and sensitizing them to the need for
cooperative efforts among households and communities in maintaining the
sanitary and public hygiene improvements provided under the project. In
particular, the risk of malaria would be reduced for the 85,000 inhabitants
of the areas covered by the component to improve N'Djamena's sanitation
infrastructure. In that component, the temporary use of two open
collectors for drainage in the two flood-prone areas pending completion of
the overall drainage system's infrastructure (para 3.12) could be a
breeding ground for mosquitoes and other vectors of disease. Since no
other practical and affordable solution could be found, these collectors
would be used as safely as possible, and the controlled use of insecticides
and other control measures would be financed under the project. During
negotiations the Government gave assurances that the use of insecticides
under the project's sanitation component will follow the Bank's guidelines
on the use of pesticides in public health projects.
E. Specialist Services
4.17      Technical assistance.  Consultants would be selected under the
Bank's Guidelines for the Use of Consultants, with qualifications and
experience acceptable to IDA, to provide various forms of technical
assistance in a number of areas: specialized management, technology
transfer and promotion of small local enterprises, public health, and
engineering. The total technical assistance required would be about 578
man-months, of which 264 would be recruited locally. A list of the
specialist services, agreed during negotiations, is at Annex 4-3.



- 29 -
4.18      Surveys and studies.  Local and international consultants (total
of 328 man-months), with qualifications and experience acceptable to IDA,
would be selected under the Bank's Guidelines for the Use of Consultants to
provide technical assistance for the design of socioeconomic studies,
surveys, and policy analysis for the component to strengthen social policy
formulation.
4.19      Non-governmental organizations.  This type of specialist
services would be equivalent to 338 man-months.
F. Procurement, Disbursements and Accounting
4.20      The procurement arrangements are summarized in Table 3.2.  A
detailed description of the procurement procedures is given in Annex 4-4.
4.21      IDA financing of contracts for civil works (limited to
sanitation infrastructure for the primary and secondary drainage) totalling
US$2.6 million equivalent, and goods (including furniture, computers,
equipment, vehicles and drugs) totalling about US$2.2 million equivalent,
representing about 87Z of the total IDA financing of contracts for civil
works and goods, would be grouped into a maximum of six major packages.
These items, suitable for international competitive bidding (ICB), would be
procured in accordance with the Bank's Guidelines for Procurement Under
IBRD Loans and IDA Credits (May 1985). Where ICB procedures are used, a
preferential margin of 15Z or the existing customs duty, whichever is
lower, over the c.i.f. prices of goods imports would be given to domestic
manufacturers in accordance with the Bank's guidelines. For works pcocured
on the basis of ICB, a preferential margin of 7.5% would be given to
bomestic contractors, also in accordance with the Bank's guidelines. For
the remaining of the total value of civil works and goods, LCB procurement
would be followed for small value contracts spaced in time and spread
geographically and estimated to cost less than US$100,000 equivalent each,
which in the aggregate would not exceed US$0.7 million and comprise (a)
construction and/or rehabilitation of health centers and services, and (b)
furniture and equipment. These items, which are not expected to interest
foreign suppliers because of the small size and the variety of each
contract, would be awarded on the basis of competitive bidding advertised
locally in accordance with procedures acceptable to IDA, provided that
(a) a copy of the draft standard bidding documents is submitted to and
found acceptable by IDA prior to approval of the first contract by IDA; (b)
eligible foreign cirms are not precluded from participating and are not
required to be incorporated in Chad in order to participate in the bidding;
(c) bids are opened in public; (d) evaluation criteria is specified with
sufficient clarity; and (e) award is made to the lowest evaluated bidder.
Items not exceeding US$15,000 and aggregating a maximum of US$200,000
equivalent could be purchased through local and international shopping on
the basis of Frice quotations obtained from at least three reliable
suppliers to ensure competitive prices. Specialist services and training
financed by IDA would be contracted in accordance with IDA's guidelines on
the use of consultants. For civil works and goods estimated at more than



- 30 -
US$100,000 equivalent each, invitations to bid and proposed award of
contracts would be reviewed by IDA prior to final award decisions. It is
estimated that this review would cover about 85Z of the value of these
contracts. For civil works and goods estimated at less than US$100,000
equivalent each, representing about 13Z of the value of these contracts,
all procurement decisions would be subject to IDA's selective post-award
review. Procurement of contracts to be financed by the Swiss Development
Cooperation, totalling US$6.7 million equivalent, would be administered by
IDA. Procurement of contracts to be financed by the other donors on a
parallel basis, totalling US$6.8 million equivalent, would be carried out
in accordance with their own procurement procedures.

4.23      Special Account.  To facilitate timely project implementation,
US$700,000 equivalent, denominated in CFA francs, would be advanced from
the IDA credit and deposited in a Special Account opened by the Government
in a local commercial bank. The amount is estimated to cover three months
of expenditures. Replenishment applications would be aggregated into
packages of at least US$100,000 equivalent. Reimbursements against
contracts below US$30,000 would be made against Certified Statements of
Expenditures (SOEs), for which documentation would be retained at the PCSU
for semi-annual audits and for random review by IDA staff during
supervision missions. Reimbursement applications would also include a
statement of account movements since the last application, with the balance



- 32 -
certified by the bank holding the account, and a reconciliation showing
that the balance represents the original amount less payments awaiting
reimbursement of small working advances. Given the availability of the
Special Account, the minimum application form for direct payment would
normally be for the equivalent of US$20,000. The Government would submit
replenishment requests to the Special Account on a monthly basis.
4.24      Accounting and auditing.  The PCSU would maintain the Special
Account, which would be subdivided into expenditures incurred for each
project component. The PCSU is setting up an accounting system, which an
independent auditor, to be recruited for the audit reports, will help
operate. During negotiations the Government gave assurances that (a) all
project accounts will be audited annually, with the exception of all
disbursements against SOEs financed under the Special Account, which will
be audited twice yearly, and an independent auditor, acceptable to IDA,
will be recruited for those purposes; (b) the annual audit reports will be
submitted to IDA for review not later than six months after the end of the
fiscal year, beginning in 1992; (c) the audit reports for SOEs will be
submitted to IDA for review by June 30 and December 31 of each year,
beginning in 1990; and (d) the audit reports will certify that the funds
were used for the purposes for which they were provided and confirm that
summary SOEs submitted as justification for disbursement correctly reflect
the detailed records maintained by the PCSU.
V. PROJECT BENEFITS AND RISKS
A. Benefits
5.01      The proposed project would be the first comprehensive attempt in
Chad to target benefits to the population groups most affected by the
disruptions of the past decade or those expected to be vulnerable to the
financial and economic adjustment programs recently initiated. In this
context, the project would make a significant contribution to improving
living conditions, creating new employment opportunities, and assisting the
Government in its efforts towards economic and financial adjustment and the
reconstruction of a sound economy. Following the country's prolonged
period of disruptions, during which the population demonstrated a
remarkable resilience, the enhanced prospect of economic recovery combined
with improved social conditions would have a highly motivational and
morale-building effect, bolstering public support for the adjustment
process and encouraging people and their communities to work together and
fully participate in the national reconstruction effort.
5.02      The project would contribute to the enhancement of job creation,
especially in urban areas where economic activities are sluggish and
rapidly deteriorating living conditions put the population most at risk.
Jobs would be created through (a) the labor-intensive activities financed
under the project (about 15,000 persons would be employed under the various
schemes over the life of the project); and (b) the credit assistance scheme
and the technical and training support for micro-enterprises (150 small
entrepreneurs and 530 micro-entrepreneurs, creating about 1,200 jobs). The



- 33 -
project would also expand accessibility to higher-quality health care and
social services for more than 150,000 persons in N'Djamena by the end of
the project. The provision of equipment, supplies, medications, and better
trained personnel is expected to more than double the utilization of health
centers in N'Djamena and Tandjile (540,000 and 360,000 inhabitants,
respectively), and improved peripheral care should reduce the bypassing of
these centers to overcrowded central or district hospitals. Reduction of
malaria and other diseases associated with poor sanitation is expected to
improve the health of 85,000 people living in the areas where the drainage
system will be restructured.   The project's techniques and innovative
approach for addressing social issues would be further assessed to ensure
sustainability and replicability wlien upscaled in nationwide programs, by
combining the findings of socioeconomic research studieq with lessons drawn
from implementing specific action plans. Moreover, the annual seminars and
workshops to be conducted under the project would allow all parties
concerned (including interested NGOs) to discuss and be informed on the
progress of implementation of the project actions, thereby ensuring their
integration into the country's development policies. The institution
building and personnel training impact of the project should also lead to a
more efficient delivery of social services in N'Djamena and Tandjile. The
project would also help the Government to promote community and private
initiatives and to collaborate more effectively with NGOs.
B. Risks
5.03      The project's main risks are related to the need to effectively
implement its diversified activities while respecting its objectives--
particularly those that address the urgent needs of disadvantaged groups--
and ensuring that these activities are compatible with the Government's
longer-term macroeconomic and sectoral objectives. All project risks are
compounded by the weak institutional situation still prevailing in Chad.
The Government is, however, strongly committed to the project, and the high
degree of mobilization by the Chadian institutions during project
preparation augurs well for the fucure.
5.04      These implementation risks are expected to be mitigated by the
following measures: (a) definition of detailed annual action plans and
careful identification of the particular target beneficiary groups, as
opposed to financing activities to be identified during project
implementation; (b) refinement and expansion of techniques already applied
effectively by NGOs or other organizations familiar with the Chadian social
environment at the "grassroots' level, to increase the chances of reaching
disadvantaged groups; (c) the setting up of a Project Coordination and
Support Unit with financial autonomy and full-time staff to ensure quick
processing and efficient handling of procurement and disbursements and to
assist the executing agencies in their relations with the donors; and (d)
provision of substantial training and technical assistance inputs to enable
existing public services to operate more efficiently. The project's
multisectoral activities require close monitoring and regular consultations
among all parties concerned, including the cofinanciers.



- 34 -
VI. AGREEMENTS REACHED AND RECOMMENDATION
6.01      During negotiations, the Government gave the following
assurances:
(a)  The Interministerial Committee and the four tet;hnical sub-
committees will be maintained throughout the project period,
under terms and conditions satisfactory to IDA (para 4.04);
(b)  The Project Coordination and Support Unit's work procedures and
relations with the executing agencies will be as agreed with
IDA; the PCSU will be staffed for the entire project period with
personnel occupying the full-time positions of Project Director
and accountant, and for the first three years will also include
a Deputy Director; and these positions will be filled at all
times with personnel whose qualifications and experience are
satisfactory to IDA (para 4.05);
(c)  The organization, functions, staffing and responsibilities of
the Health-Social Unit and the Sanitation Infrastructure Unit
will be satisfactory to IDA (para 4.06);
(d)  The Goverunent will (i) submit to IDA for review annual reports
on project implementation and expenditures, the first report by
September 30, 1991: (ii) undertake with IDA and the other donors
annual reviews of the progress of implementation, starting not
later than November 1, 1991, and every year thereafter; (iii)
agree with IDA, not later than December 31 of each year, on the
next annual budgetary program aggregating the annual action
plans for each component and each executing agency; and (iv)
submit a project completion report within six months of the
credit closing date (para 4.07);
.e)  The interest rate under the credit scheme will be 12? until June
30, 1991, and increased to 132 thereafter, with an added front-
end service fee of 2Z in both cases; the interest rate will be
adjusted not later than December 31, 1991, on the basis of the
findings of a banking sector review study and pursuant to the
financial performance of the credit scheme and the prevailing
commercial interest rates; and the contract with the NGO for
management of the line of credit will be as agreed with IDA
(para 4.09);
(f)  The three integrated health-social centers, three maternity
centers and three dispensaries to be built in N'Djamena will be
staffed as agreed with IDA and located on the sites already
found acceptable; a cost recovery scheme based on a system of
fixed fees per new episode of illness will be introduced for the
services provided by the three maternities constructed under the
project, and in the health centers supplied with essential drugs
under the project, and will at all times be satisfactory to IDA;
and the Health-Social Unit will be staffed at al.l times with



- 35 -
personnel whose qualifications and experience are satisfactory
to IDA (para 4.12);
(g) The Government's operating budgets for N'Djamena's PHC and
social services network and for Tandjile's regional health
services will be increased, starting from their 1990 base, by at
least 102 each year in 1991, 1992 and 1993, a rate in line with
the budgetary provisions under the third PFP 1990-92 (paras 4.12
and 4.13);
(h)  The qualifications and experience of the technical personnel of
the Sanitation Infrastructure Unit and the arrangements with the
municipal services will at all times be satisfactory to IDA
(para 4.14);
(i) Before undertaking the socioeconomic studies and household
surveys, the Government will submit for IDA's approval the
annual programs, including terms of reference, schedule, and
arrangements for their dissemination and implementation (para
4.15);
(j) The Government will review with IDA the recommendations of the
policy studies and agree on action plans for their
implementation (para 4.15);
(k) The use of insecticides under the project's sanitation component
will follow the Bank's guidelines on the use of pesticides in
public health projects (para 4.16); and
(1) All project accounts will be audited annually, with the
exception of all disbursements against SOEs financed under the
Special Account, which will be audited twice yearly, and an
independent auditor, acceptable to IDA. will be recruited for
those purposes; the annual audit reports will be submitted to
IDA for review not later than six months after the end of the
fiscal year, beginning in 1992; the audit reports for SOEs will
be submitted to IDA for review not later than six months after
end of fiscal year, beginning in 1992; the audit reports for
SOEs will be submitted to IDA for review by June 30 and December
31 of each year, beginning in 1990; and the audit reports will
certify that the funds were used for the purposes for which they
were provided and confirm that summary SOEs submitted as
justification for disbursement correctly reflect the detailed
records maintained by the PCSU (para 4.24).
6.02      The following are conditions of credit effectiveness:
(a) Contracts with the two consulting firms involved in the sub-
components to improve N'Djamena's PHC and social services
network (para 4.12), and to strengthen regional health services
in Tandjile (para 4.13), and with the NGO responsible for the



- 36 -
community participation program (para 4.14) are satisfactory to
IDA and have been signed; and
(b) The Coordinator recruited under the sub-component on technical
assistance for micro-enterprises (para 4.10) and the engineer
and the head foreman recruited for the Sanitation Infrastructure
Unit (para 4.14) have taken up their duties.
6.03      Conditions of disbursement on the credit assistance and
management support sub-component are that (a) the USAID grant has become
effective; and (b) the contract with the NGO for management of the line of
credit has been signed (para 4.09).
6.04      Recommendation.  Subject to the above terms and conditions, the
proposed project would be suitable for an IDA credit of US$13.4 million
equivalent to the Republic of Chad on standard IDA terms, with 40 years'
maturity.

TCHAD
PROJET D'ACTIONS POUR LE DEVELOPPEMENT SOCIAL
PLAN D'ACTION POUR STIMULER LA CREATION D'EMPLOI
1.        Obiectifs.  Cette composante vise A la mise en place de mesures
qui doivent contribuer, dans le cadre de la preparation d'une strategie
globale de creation d'emploi, a la realisation des objectifs specifiques
immediats suivants:
(a)  Promouvoir l'acces des petits entrepreneurs a un systeme de
credit-assistance & des taux d'interet et frais bancaires du
marche (sans subventions), a l'information-formation
(technologie et savoir-faire), et aux marches-debouches
(equipement, approvisionnement et demandes interieure et
exterieure);
(b) Realiser une meilleure articulation entre la promotion des
micro-entreprises (MiE) et le processus de developpement global
de l'economie (creation d'emploi, diversification des activites,
valorisation des ressources locales);                I
(c) Ameliorer la reinsertion et l'insertion dans le march4 de
l'emploi et l'adequation entre offre et demande par
qualification.
2.   Pour faciliter la realisation de ces objectifs, le Plan d'action de
cette composante slarticule autour de trois programmes qui s'executeront
sur une periode d'environ trois ans, et des etudes et recherches etalees
sur cinq ans pour aider a la preparation de mesures promotionnelles pour
faciliter la creation d'emploi; ces actions seront analysees & l'annexe 3-
4 dans le cadre des etudes visant a renforcer la formulation des politiques
sociales. Ces trois programmes devraient en particulier permettre, a la
fin du projet, d'aborder sur des bases plus solides, la conception et mise
en place d'une politique coherente de promotion de la micro-entreprise et
le renforcement de l'Office de la main d'oeuvre, consideres comme deux
elements-clef d'une strategie de creation d'emploi coherente et efficace.
Ces trois programmes concernent:
(I) La promotion du credit-assistance aux MiE (qui
poursuivrait et diversifierait le Projet Entreprises
Privees -PEP-).
(II) La mise en place d'un systeme-reseau d'appui technique couvrant
progressivement l'ensemble du Tchad.
(III) Une action specifique de conseils pour aider les employes du



- 41 -
ANNEXE 3-1
Page 2 sur 19
secteur public licencies (pour cause de programme d'ajustement)
a se reinserer dans la vie active.
3.        Cette composante du projet a ete evaluOe & 1.4 millierds de
FCFA, incluant les provisions pour risques et inflation, equivalant & 4.7
millions de dollars E.U. L'Annexe 3-6 donne tous les details sur la
structure des coats: (a) pour le premier programme, le coat total s'4lbve a
880 millions de FCFA, dont 410 pour l'assistance technique, 130 de coat
local (y compris le personnel), et 160 millions pour la provision reserv4e
aux prOts; (b) pour le deuxieme programme, le coat total de 410 millions de
FCFA se decompose en 110 millions pour le transfert de technologie et ;90
millions pour l'assistance technique; et (c) pour le troisieme programme,
le coat total de 120 millions comprend 50 millions d'assistance et 50
millions de coet local. Le reste de la contribution locale se limite a
fourtiir des fonds sans interets pour mettre en place une ligne de cr6dit
renouvelable pour les microentreprises, mais qui prend en charge les
risques de default ou de non-remboursement.
LA PROMOTION DU CREDIT-ASSISTANCE AUX HICRO-ENTREPRISES.
4.        Les objectifs specifiques Pt le contenu de ce programme de
promotion du credit-assistance aux MiE sont decrits dans le document
technique intitule La promotion de la micro-entreprise, prepare pour ce
Rapport d'evaluation. Neanmuins, ce rapport decrit un programme beaucoup
plus large que celui retenu dans le projet et qui tient compte des
financements disponibles. Les objectifs sp6cifiques qui ont ete retenus
comme prioritaires pour le projet sont donc les suivants:
(a) developper l'accbs au credit-assistance des petits e.atrepreneurs
(MiE) en mettant en application une methodologie d'approche
adaptee a leurs problemes et leurs capacites afin de faire face
progressivement & l'acces au credit bancaire normal; et
diversifier l'origine des emprunteurs geographiquement et
sectoriellement.
(b)  ameliorer les performances de l'equipe en charge du programme
PEP; et developper ainsi une capacite locale de gestion d'un
programme de promotion du cr6dit-assistance aux MiE qui soit
viable au bout de trois ans d'actions du projet.
(c)  coordonner l'assistance prevue, notamment A la gestion, avec
celle plus technique qui sera fournie par le systeme technique
d'appui (par. 10); et intensifier les contacts (et actions
concertees) avec les autres actions concernees par la promotion
des MiE, notamment celles des ONG.
(d)  developper l'intervention des banques commerciales et de
developpement vers la promotion des MiE; et aider
l'Administration a mieux percevoir les problemes des MiE et
preparer une strategie de promotion plus ciblee.



- 42 -
ANNEXE 3-1
Page 3 sur 19
4.        Pour ce faire, le projet PEP, actuellement confie a une ONG -
VITA localisee aux USA -, sera ajuste afin d'etre en mesure de realiser les
taches prioritaires suivantes, la mise en place du programme etant resumee
dans le chronogramme ci-joint:
(a)  Mise en place d'une methodologie d'approche adaptee aux profils
d'un micro-entrepreneur. Cette methodologie est decrite dans un
document technique prepare par l'ONG responsable du programme.
Elle tire les le;ons de quatre annees d'exp4rience a developper
I'accas au crddit pour les entreprises petites et moyennes (PME)
lans le cadre du projet PEP et les etudes faites sur ce secteur,
notamment par l'ONG britannique OXFAM en ce qui concerne les
specificites du secteur informel. L'ONG responsable du
programme financd par le projet aura & former I cette methode
l'equipe locale chargee du programme et notamment les charges de
prets affectes ou recrutes a N'Djamena et & Moundou (ob une
antenne devrait Otre ouverte sur financement PNUD) pour se
concentrer au credit-assistance aux MiE. Cette methode mettra
l'accent sur l'approche des problames en groupe sachant que le
pret a un micro-entrepreneur exigera la constitution d*un groupe
d'environ cinq co-responsables (garantie collective pour obtenir
le credit, possibilites d'achats et de travaux en commun), la
sensibilisation par les medias, les visites sur le lieu .e
travail, et la coordination avec le systeme d'appui technique
(par. 10).
(b)  Diversification par type. secteur, et localisation.  Le
programme developpera des operations visant a assister une large
variete d'entreprises afin de les aider dans leurs besoins
immediats, de renforcer le tissu d'unit4s productives a tous les
niveaux de technologie (passant de la MiE & la PME), et donc de
diversifier les types d'emplois et de produits qui pourraient
Otre promus. Le programme continuera donc les operations d'un
montant relativement eleve (plus de 25.000 dollars EU) et
eligible au credit bancaire standard, qui seront co-financees
avec une banque commerciale locale (comme le prevoit l'accord
deja signe par VITA avec la BTCD). L'antenne prevue a Moundou
permettra d'atteindre les MiE nombreuses dans les regions du Sud
et renforcer ainsi l'effet du programme et contrebalancer celui
de la restructuration de la filiere coton. De toute fagon, on
pourrait utiliser des ONG deja installees pour selectionner des
candidats potentiels et les aider a preparer leurs dossiers; un
membre de l'equipe centrale pourrait se rendre regulierement
dans d'autres villes eventuellement, pour recueillir ces
dossiers.
5.   Le Gouvernement s'est engage a donner tout son appui au developpe-
ment de ce programme. Celui qui est en cours -PEP- a rencontre des
problemes resultant de la confusion qui slest repandue parmi les



- 43 -
ANNEXE 3-1
Page 4 sur 19
beneficiaires potentiels entre le role d'une ONG pergue comme devant
apporter une assistance benevole et celui du credit bancaire qui exige des
paiements de fra_.s et d'int6rfts.  Afin de donner toutes ses chances au
prograanme finance par le projet, des campagnes d'information et de
sensibilisation a tous niveaux, sous la tutelle de la Direction de
l'industrie et les Chambres de commerce, d'industrie et d'artisanat, seront
entreprises das le debut du projet; elles seront basees sur les themes
suivants. Pour que le credit A toutes les entreprises -grandes, moyennes,
petites et micros- puisse a l'avenir se developper au Tchad dans des
conditions rapides mais satisfaisantes, c'est-a-dire avec un credit sans
subventions par rapport aux cotts de mobilisation de l'4pargne, tous les
entrepreneurs, quels que soient leur statut, doivent accepter de payer des
interets et frais bancaires normaux sur tous les credits qu'ils
contractent. I1 est donc essentiel de distinguer, dans ce programme,
l'aspect credit pur soumis & la legislation normale bancaire et aux frais
normaux de gestion et de suivi des dossiers d'avec l'aspect assistance
octroyee aux petits et micro entrepreneurs pour ameliorer les performances
de leurs entreprises. Le programme offre donc deux types d'appui: le
premier vise a ce que les tout petits projets financierement rentables
aient acces a du credit & un taux qui se rapprochr progressivement du taux
bancaire normal et non au credit informel a des taux d'int4rOt usuraire, et
le second vise a fournir une assistance massive mais gratuite a la gestion
pour amener ces projets & des conditions normales de fonctionnement et de
rentabilite financibre. Compte tenu des caracteristiques des
microentreprises informelles; il est en outre necessaire d'experimenter
avec des methodes d'approche basees sur celles habituellement utilisees par
les ONG; de plus, VITA est la seule institution capable de demarrer une
telle experimention au Tchad immediatement.  C'est donc pour des raisons
contingentes et donc temporaires dues A la situation propre du Tchad que le
programme est enti6rement mais temporairement gere par une ONG Otrang6re.
6.        Le Plan d'action pour cette composante (voir tableau 3.4 ci-
joint) implique la mise en place de deux elements importants:
(a)  Restructuration de l'atuipe chargee du PEP.  Le personnel
expat-:e de VITA qui assurent la gestion du projet PEP, co-
finance par l'USAID et le Gouvernement, sera charge de mettre en
place cette restructuration. Il est prevu qu'il devra quitter
ses fonctions a plein temps sur place apr4s environ deux ans
pour poursuivre eventuellement une assistance par visites
ponctuelles. L'equipe actuelle de N'Djamena de 28 membres sera
restructuree; le personnel present qui a d4j& ete teste par le
projet PEP sera soit realloue aux nouvelles positions definies
dans le projet, soit remercie si leurs qualifications ne sont
plus conformes au nouvel organigramme.  I1 sera cre4 une equipe
d'environ 21 membres (dont 2 cadres et 9 charges ou
gestionnaires de prOts) residant a N'Djamena. Les autres
pourront Oventuellement faire partie de l'equipe A installer A
Moundou sur financement PNUD. Les frais de fonctionnement
continueront d'etre finances sur un don de l'USAID.



- 44 -
ANNEXE 3-1
Page 5 sur 19
(b)  Modification des conditions d'octroi des prets.   I1 sera etabli
une ligne de credit sur financement IDA pour l'octroi de prOts
aux microentreprises dans le cadre du projet; elle completera
les transactions sur les prets en cours resultant du projet PEP.
Cette ligne recevra toutes les transactions financieres
concernant les prAts - principe de la ligne de credit
renouvelable. Les termes des prOts octroyes par le projet
seront bases sur un taux d'int4ret unique de 122 jusqu'au 30
juin 1991 et de 13% aprea, et des annuites de remboursement
fonction du type de projet. Neanmoins, les conditions d'octroi
du credit devraient etre reexaminees au plus tard le 31 decembre
1991 lorsque seront disponibles les conclusions de 1'6tude sur
le secteur bancaire, prevue dans le cadre des accords avec le
FMI et la Banque mondiale et les premi'res performances de cette
ligne de cr6dit. Des cotts de gestion et de suivi des dossiers
seront percus et varieront suivant la taille du pret. Ces
conditions sont decrites dans le document technique et resumees
dans le tableau 3.1 ci-dessous. Les conditions de garantie
seront ajustees pour pouvoir etre adaptees au contexte d'un

PROGRAMME D'ASSISTANCE AUX LICENCIES DU SECTEUR PUBLIC POUR LEUR
REINSERTION
17.       Le programme sera ouvert en priorite aux personnes licencies
depuis 1986 dans le cadre du programme de restructuration de la filibre
coton (environ 1,700 agents de la COTONTCHAD et de l'ONDR), aux personnes
qui pourraient etre licenci4es dans le cadre des programmes de
restructuration en cours ou en preparation, et finalement a toute personne
cherchant 'n emploi.  Un service capable de fournir une assistance a ceux
qui le souhaitent pour leur reinsertion dans la vie active sera donc
developpe dans le cadre du projet au sein de l'Office national de la main
d'oeuvre (ONAMO). Le programme oriente vers le renforcement institutionnel
permettra donc de creer une capacit4 d'accueil et d'orientation
operationnelle et permanente pour l'insertion et la reinsertion des
chercheurs dtemploi. Les objectifs specifiques suivants ont ete retenus
poui le programme d'assistance aux licencies:
(a) accueillir en priorite les employes du secteur public ayant
perdu ou qui perdront leur emploi a cause des programmes
d'ajustement decidts ou induits par le gouvernement et qui sont
a la recherche d'un emploi.
(b) orienter les chercheurs d'emploi selon leurs capacites vers des
projets bancables de creation d'emploi ou vers des postes de
travail disponibles.
(c)  ddvelopper une capacite locale pour identifier les besoins
immddiats du marche du travail et a ameliorer l1'adquation a
court terme entre offre et demande d'emploi par qualification.
On notera que l'assistance aux licencies du secteur public se limitera a
une action specifique de conseil, car ces licencies auront a leur
disposition les indemnites obtenues dans le cadre des obligations legales
des entreprises publiques.

place au sein de 1'ONAMO renforcera les bureaux a N'Djamena et Moundou, ce
dernier rayonnant sur Sarh et couvrant ainsi les zones a vocation
cotonniere les plus touchges par les licenciements. Les taches
prioritaires a realiser sont (voir chronogramme ci-joint, tableau 3.6):
- maintenir a jour la liste des licencids.

- etablir un systeme d'interviews et de tests.

d'emploi.

d'appui technique (par. 3 et 10).
- etablir et actualiser les grilles d'orientation par

l'Annexe 4-1 qui explicite l'ensemble des procedures retenues et des
institutions impliquees dans l'administration du projet. Le tableau 3.7
ci-joint schematise la gestion de cette composante. Dans cette composante
sur la promotion de l'emploi, pour en effectuer les taches, dont la plupart
sont executees en liaison avec des ONG, et preparer une strategie, le

coordination du projet et d'autro part, par un Sous-Comite technique charR6
de la promotion de l'emploi, pr4sidO par le Directeur g4n4ral de
l'industrie, od seront pris en compte les interets specifiques que
devraient porter I ce projet les Departements er. charge de l'industrie, du
travail et de l'emploi, de l'enseignement technique et aussi du commerce et
du credit. Ce Sous-Comite suivra l'execution technique des quatre
programmes definis ci-dessus tout en assurant la tutelle technique directe
du premier programme sur le credit aux microentreprises. I1 devra donc
collationner tous les rapports techniques emanant des diverses agences
d'execution impliquees; rappelons que ces agences -Cellule d'appui
technique, ONG en charge du programme de credit et 1'ONAMO- ont la
responsabilit6 de mettre en oeuvre les programmes sous la tutelle
financibre de la Cellule de coordination et de soutien du projet. Elles
soumettront chaque mois le rapport de mise en oeuvre (critdres de
performance), chaque semestre un rapport d'execution de ces programmes et
chaque ann4e un programme annuel de travail qui sera transmis pour
information et approbation a l'Association (Annexe 4-1).
24.       Le premier rapport annuel et le premier seminaire se
concentreront sur le demarrage du programme et les problemes Eventuels
rencontrEs. La premiEre annee, on utilisera les resultats de l'enqu@te sur
le secteur informel prive urbain pour faire une premiere analyse de la
problematique de la promotion des MiE. Apres trois ans d'execution, le
dernier rapport et le dernier seminaire prepareront des recommandations
pour la mise en place d'une strategie de promotion de la micro-entreprise
et de renforcement de l'Office national de la main d'oeuvre et un programme
d'actions generalisables A grande echelle.

TCHAD
PROJET D'ACTIONS POUR LE DEVELOPPEMENT SOCIAL
PLAN D'ACTION POUR RENFORCER LES SERVICES SANITAIRES ET SOCIAUX
DESCRIPTION GENERALE DU SYSTEME
1.        Objectifs.  Cette composante vise a la mise en place de mesures
qui doivent, dans le cadre de la preparation d'une strategie de
developpement des services de sante et du developpement social, contribuer
a realiser les objectifs specifiques suivants:
i)   Mettre en place une organisation sanitaire et de developpement
communautaire qui permette aux populations de se prendre
progressivement en t:harge;
ii)  Rer.forcer les services sociaux et de sante de base
dans une approche integree de toutes les actions
visant a ameliorer le bien-atre familial;
iii) Developper un systeme de services de sante qui
permettent de donner la priorite a la sante de la mere
et de l'enfant et reduire les inegalites regionales et
sociales dans la couverture sanitaire;
iv) Ameliorer a tous les niveaux la gestion des ressources
humaines, materielles et financieres allouees aux
services sociaux et de sante.
2.        Pour permettre la realisation de ces objectifs, le projet a
selectionne pour cette composante un plan d'action qui tient compte (a) des
zones ayant le besoin le plus pressant de renforcement des soins de sante
et dtveloppement communautaire de base, et qui n'etaient pas incluses dans
d'autres programmes sur financement exterieur, et (b) des actions qui
permettront de renforcer la maitrise des problemes socio-sanitaires du
Tchad et d'aborder sur de bonnes bases, apres trois ans de projet, la
conception d'une politique de developpement social et de sante, et la
preparation et mise en place d'un eventuel projet de sante-population a
plus long terme qui pourrait aussi etre co-finance par l'IDA. Les deux
programmes suivants ont donc ete selectionnes:
I)   Renforcement a N'Djamena des services de sante et d'aide au
developpement social et communautaire.
IT)  Renforcement au Tandjile de la gestion de la prefecture
medicale et de la qualite des services publics de sante.



- 60 -
ANNEXE 3-2
Page 2 sur 16
Des etudes et recherches pour fournir les bases de definition d'une
politique plus coherente de sante et developpement communautaire ont ete
prevues dans la composante axee sur la formulation des politiques sociales.
Ces etudes et recherches constitueront donc en fait un troisieme programme
qui completera les deux precedents (Annexe 3-4).
3.        La presente composante a ete evaluee a 2.4 milliards de FCFA,
incluant les provisions pour risques et inflation et equivalent a 8.5
millions de dollars EU; le troisieme programme etant pris en charge par le
budget de la composante sur la foL-mulation des politiques sociales (Annexe
3-4). L'Annexe 3-6 donne tous les details sur la structure des couts.
Pour le premier programme, le coat total se monte a 1.6 milliards de FCFA,
dont 340 millions pour l'assistance technique, 100 millions de FCFA pour le
fonctionnement local (le personnel qualifie etant finance sur budget des
Ministeres de la sante publique, MSP, et des affaires sociales, MASPF), et
380 millions en medicaments essentiels (dont 30% seront recuperes par
l'Etat a partir des recouvrements de coats). De meme, le coat total de 930
millions de FCFA du deuxieme programme se decompose en 210 millions de FCFA
en assistance technique, 210 millions de FCFA en fonctionnement local sans
personnel, et 330 millions de FCFA en medicaments essentiels (dont 30%
seront recouverts a partir des versements des malades). La contribution du
Gouvernement est importante dans cette composante; d'abord, il s'est engage
a fournir tout le personnel de sante et social necessaire. Il s'est engage
.galement a fournir les terrains sur lesquels seront batis les
infrastructures medico-sociales prevues dans le projet et les batiments a
rehabiliter pour loger certaines activites de ce programme; ces dernieres
contributions n'ont pas ete evaluees en equivalent monetaire.
RENFORCEMENT DES SERVICES DE SANTE ET DE L'AIDE AU DEVELOPPEMENT
COMMUNAUTAIRE A N'DJAMENA.
4.        Les objectifs et le contenu detaille de ce programme sont
decrits dans les document technique prepare par la mission d'evaluation et
intitule -Composante sur le Renforcement des services de sante et de l'aide
au developpement communautaire a N'Djamena- (par le Docteur Antoine
Degremont, consultant et Directeur de l'Institut tropical suisse). Les
objectifs qui ont ete retenus comme prioritaires pour le projet sont les
suivants:
- etendre et ameliorer les infrastructures des r-rvices de sante et de
developpement communautaire et generaliser l'utilisation du medicament
essentiel pour augmenter l'accessibilite, l'acceptabilite, et la couverture
des prestations des services de base sur la ville de N'Djamena.
- ameliorer les capacites de planification, de gestion, d'execution, de
supervision et d'evaluation du personnel des centres sociaux et medicaux de
N'Djamena.
- ameliorer la qualite et l'efficience des prestations des services de
sante et de developpement communautaire, avec notamment une priorite donnee



- 61 -
ANNEXE 3-2
Page 3 sur 16
a la sante maternelle et infantile et a l'education pour la sante
familiale, par une collaboration permanente des structures sanitaires et
sociales et la mise en place d'un processus de sante communautaire.
Ces objectifs ne pourront evidemment etre atteints qu'apres une periode
plus longue que celle du projet qui ne constitue qu'une phase pilote
prealable a l'evaluation de programmes sectoriels.
5.        Pour ameliorer la qualite des services de sante de base, une
action clef du projet sera l'experimentation et diffusion d'un systeme de
distribution des medicamaents essentiels et de recouvrement des coats 1/.
Ce systeme (par. 6) sera progressivement mis en place dans les maternites
et les centres de sante construits ou renoves par le projet a N'Djamena; il
demarrera des qu'un district medico-social d'arrondissement fonctionnera
sous la responsabilite de la Cellule d'execution du programme medico-
social (voir par. 11). Chaque centre (maternite ou dispensaire) renove
disposera d'une liste des wrdicaments essentiels autorises et d'un guide
(ou manuel) therapeutique donnant les conditions d'utilisation de ces
medicaments. Chaque mois, sur la base des statistiques de soins du mois
precedent (frequence des maladies diagnostiquees), l'infirmier(e)
responsable du centre avaiuera et commandera les besoins mensuels en
medicaments essentiels a la Cellule medico-sociale (collationnes par le
district medico-social, voir par.10). Cette Cellule sera chargee, dans le
cadre du projet, de gerer les commandes et la distribution des medicaments
essentiels necessaires aux centres de sante, dispensaires et maternites de
quartier de N'Djamena; le stockage et conditionnement etant assure par la
Pharmacie centrale d'approvisionnement -PASP- (moyennant un amenagement des
locaux prevu par le projet). La Cellule medico-sociale utilisera les
appels d'offres internationaux en DCI (denomination commune internation-
ale) excluant tout monopole d'approvisionnement; en l'absence d'une
politique nationale du medicament essentiel, que le projet pourra aider a
definir et mettre en oeuvre, elle utilisera les procedures d'achats que le
Gouvernement a definies avec le Projet Sante du VIeme FED. Pour eviter de
se trouver sai,s medicaments au debut du projet, une procedure de
consultations rapides par telex aupres de quelques fournisseurs agrees par
1'IDA est suggeree pour une premiere commande equivalent aux besoins
grossierement estimes sur un an.
6.        De meme, en l'absence d'une politique nationale de recouvrement
des couts (voir renvoi 1/), on utilisera la methode prevue a l'arrete
conjoint du Ministre de la sante et de celui des finances qui autorise un
systeme interimaire de recouvrement pour certains projets, dont le PADS.
Pour chaque episode de maladie, le malade aura a se procurer pour avoir
acces aux services medicaux (visite et medicaments essentiels) un ticket
(que l'on pouurait fixer a 200 FCFA a titre indicatif) par episode medical
1/ Bien entendu, si pendant la rariode de mise en oeuvre du projet, le
Gouvernement se decide sur une m;thode nationale de recouvrement des coats,
cette methode sera immediatement appliquee dans les centres rehabilites par
le projet et meme testee si le Gouvernement le souhaite.



- 62 -
ANNEXE 3-2
Page 4 sur 16
et valable dans un centre renove; a la maternite, ce ticket pourrait etre
fix; a 800 FCFA pour une femme enceinte, y compris les soins prenataux et
les frais d'accouchement. Ce ticket lui sera fourni par l'infirmier(e)
responsable qui se sera procure un carnet a souches aupres du Bureau
(guichet) de la tresorerie du quartier. L'assistant(e) social dil centre
(s'il est du type integri ou du centre social designe du quartier) decidera
si un malade est indigent et lui fournira un ticket special pour des soins
gratuits. Les criteres d'identification des indigents pourraient etre
fixis periodiquement entre le Service social de la Mairie de N'Djamena, les
responsables du quartier, les representants des communautes et le personnel
des services sociaux. La Direction de la Trisorerie devra proceder a
l'impression de carnets a souche specifiques aux centres renovis par le
projet. Le Gouvernement s'est engage a reverser les recettes de ce systeme
interimaire aux services du MSP (sante de base) pour leur permettre de
faire face aux augmentations necessaires de leur fonctionnement, avec
utilisation prioritaire pour le renouvellement du stock de medicaments
essentiels. I1 est bien entendu essentiel que le processus et modalitis de
mise en place soient prepares en coordination avec les autres projets qui
eux aussi mettent en place un systime de recouvrement des coats.
7.        Pour ameliorer les infrastructures socio-medicales de base, on a
dae plus prevu les actions d'investissement suivantes:
- construire trois maternitis de 16 lits chacune (Farcha, Hilli-Leclerc, et
Paris-Congo).
- construire trois centres medico-sociaux integres (Hilli-Leclerc, Paris-
Congo, et Ragouta-Djemaal).
- construire trois dispensaires de quartier (Ndjari, Diguel-Est, et Diguel-
Nord).
- completer la rinovation en cours de quatre centres sociaux et d'un
dispensaire et la cloture de quatre dispensaires .
- fournir et completer les iquipements necessaires (mobilier, materiel
medico-sanitaire, materiel iducatif) des centres sociaux et niidicaux i
partir d'une liste-type de dotation.
- amenager et ranover des locaux administratifs pour stocker a la PASP les
medicaments essentiels pour les centres de N'Djamena et pour accueillir la
Cellule d'execution de la composante medico-sociale de N'Djamena.
On trouvera la localisation de ces centres sur la carte en appendice.
8.        Pour amiliorer les capacitis professionnelles du personnel des
centres medico-sociaux, des dispensaires et des trois maternites de
quartier, on a privu les actions suivantes:
- definir de facon precise et coherente les roles, taches, et
responsabilitis de chacun des membres des equipes medicales et sociales.



- 63 -
ANNEXE 3-2
Page 5 sur 16
- diffuser une methode de travail basee sur une identification des
objectifs et critares de performance pour toutes les activites assignees au
centre, une estimation des charges de travail, des normes budgatairen,
d'equipement et personnel et une programmation hebdomadaire des activites a
realiser.
- recycler et former en continu le personnel et les encadreurs a ces
methodes et a la maniere d'executer chaque tache assignee.
- developper une approche par equipe dans chaque centre, avec auto-
evaluation et discussion en groupe des problemes et des suggestions.
- renforcer les supports logistiques aux centres; notamment au niveau de la
formation-recyclage, du systeme de rfeirence en gynicologie obstetrique et
en pidiatrie, de l'utilisation du medicament essentiel (guide therapeuti-
que), de la gestion des approvisionnements (recouvrement des coats) et du
personnel.
- promouvoir des programmes ciblis sur le bien-etre familial et l'iducation
sanitaire de base (avec priorite a la nutrition et maternite sans risque)
et les contacts avec la (ou les) communaute(s) (visites i domicile).
- identifier le rythme de generalisation progressive des activitis
spicifiques i diffuser apris familiarisation du personnel; il est crucial
de limiter au debut le nombre d'activitis et de programmes nouveaux; une
provision dans le projet permettra la mise en place ulterieure de
programmes qui se reveleront nicessaires. Mais surtout on pourra intigrer
progressivement des activites financies par d'autres bailleurs de fonds.
9.        Compte tenu du caractere innovatif et experimental de certaines
approches diveloppies dans les centres renoves du projet, un systeme
spicial de priparation et suivi-ivaluation a ete mis en place; il est base
sur la proerammation fonctionnel'e des taches et des taux de couverture qui
ont ite adoptas pour difinir la structure des installations et du personnel
des centres (voir les documents cechniques joints pour le ditail sur la
programmation de ces activitis de base). De plus, la Cellule medico-
sociale pourra proposer des actions de recherche opirationnelle en fonction
des problemes rencontris durant la mise en oeuvre des activites
prioritaires. En particulier, on suivra comment cette approche
intersectorielle de developpement de la sante communautaire est percue par
le personnel des deux ministeres (MSP et MASPF) et par la population. On
evaluera 1'adiquation des critires de performance et des programmations
hebdomadaires, la pertinence des indicateurs et des statistiques, le role
expirimental de coordination des actions midico-sociales donne aux
districts, voir ci-dessous). Plus giniralement, on ivaluera apres trois
ans de projet les rapports cout-efficaciti des taches assignees, notamment
suivi des personnes a risque, rehabilitation nutritionnelle, et actions de
sante communautaire.
